// NB: For many call sites, it is not strictly necessary to check all of\n179: // these relationships (for example, for forward convolution, we compute\n180: // the size of output ourselves, so we don't actually need to check\n181: // output.  However, writing a single function that does everything\n182: // means we get to reuse it for both forwards and all backwards\n183: // variants, even when the set of \"real\" inputs varies.  The magic of\n184: // relational computing!\n185: //\n186: // (There is one downside, which is that it is slightly harder to write\n187: // error messages which are able to distinguish between real inputs\n188: // (which the user can change) and computed inputs (which the user can\n189: // only indirectly affect).  It would be an interesting exercise to\n190: // come up with a general framework to handle such situations.)\n191: inline void convolution_shape_check(\n192:     CheckedFrom c,\n193:     const check_args(c, padding, input->dim() - 2, \"padding\");\n197:   check_args(c, stride, padding.size(), \"stride\");\n198:   check_args(c, dilation, padding.size(), \"dilation\");\n199: \n200:   // weight);\n206: \n207:   // TODO: check that output->size() matches output_sizes\n208:   // TODO: check that weight matches output->sizes()\n209:   checkSameDim(c, input, output);\n210: }\n211: \n212: // NB: conv_output_size and conv_input_size are not bijections,\n213: // as conv_output_size loses information; this is why conv_input_size\n214: // takes an extra output_padding argument to resolve the ambiguity.\n215: \n216: template <typename T>\n217: inline std::vector<T> _conv_output_size(\n218:     ArrayRef<T> input_size, ArrayRef<T> weight_size,\n219:     ArrayRef<T> padding, ArrayRef<T> stride, ArrayRef<T> dilation = ArrayRef<T>()\n220: ) {\n221:   // ASSERT(input_size.size() > 2)\n222:   // ASSERT(input_size.size() == weight_size.size())\n223:   bool has_dilation = !dilation.empty();\n224:   auto dim = input_size.size();\n225:   std::vector<T> output_size(dim);\n226:   output_size[0] = input_size[input_batch_size_dim];\n227:   output_size[1] = weight_size[weight_output_channels_dim];\n228:   for (const auto d : c10::irange(2, dim)) {\n229:     auto dilation_ = has_dilation ? dilation[d - 2] : 1;\n230:     auto kernel = dilation_ * (weight_size[d] - 1) + 1;\n231:     output_size[d] = (input_size[d] + (2 * padding[d - 2]) - kernel) / stride[d - 2] + 1;\n232:   }\n233:   return output_size;\n234: }\n235: \n236: inline {\n240:   return _conv_output_size(input_size, weight_size, padding, stride, dilation);\n241: }\n242: \n243: inline std::vector<c10::SymInt> conv_output_size(\n244:     SymIntArrayRef input_size, padding, stride, dilation);\n248: }\n249: \n250: template <typename T>\n251: std::vector<T> _conv_input_size(\n252:     ArrayRef<T> output_size, ArrayRef<T> weight_size,\n253:     ArrayRef<T> padding, ArrayRef<T> output_padding, ArrayRef<T> stride, ArrayRef<T> dilation, T groups\n254: ) {\n255:   // ASSERT(output_size.size() > 2)\n256:   // ASSERT(output_size.size() == weight_size.size())\n257: sites, it is not strictly necessary to check all of\\n179: // these relationships (for example, for forward convolution, we compute\\n180: // the size of output ourselves, so we don't actually need to check\\n181: // output.  However, writing a single function that does everything\\n182: // means we get to reuse it for both forwards and all backwards\\n183: // variants, even when the set of \\\"real\\\" inputs varies.  The magic of\\n184: // relational computing!\\n185: //\\n186: // (There is one downside, which is that it is slightly harder to write\\n187: // error messages which are able to distinguish between real inputs\\n188: // (which the user can change) and computed inputs (which the user can\\n189: // only indirectly affect). weight_size,\\n219:     ArrayRef<T> padding, ArrayRef<T> stride, ArrayRef<T> dilation = ArrayRef<T>()\\n220: ) {\\n221:   // ASSERT(input_size.size() > 2)\\n222:   // ASSERT(input_size.size() == input_size[input_batch_size_dim];\\n227:   output_size[1] = weight_size[weight_output_channels_dim];\\n228:   for (const auto d : c10::irange(2, dim)) {\\n229:     auto dilation_ = has_dilation ? Used on pad, stride and dilation\n156: static void check_args(CheckedFrom c, IntArrayRef args, size_t expected_size, const char* arg_name)\n157: {\n158:   TORCH_CHECK(args.size() <= // NB: For many call sites, it is not strictly necessary to check all of\n179: // these relationships (for example, for forward convolution, we compute\n180: // the size of output ourselves, so we don't actually need to check\n181: // output.  However, writing a single function that does everything\n182: // means we get to reuse it for both forwards and all backwards\n183: // variants, even when the set of \"real\" inputs varies.  The magic of\n184: // relational computing!\n185: //\n186: // (There is one downside, which is that it is slightly harder to write\n187: // error messages which are able to distinguish between real inputs\n188: // (which the user can change) and computed inputs (which the user can\n189: // only indirectly affect).  It would be an interesting exercise to\n190: // come up with a general framework to handle such situations.)\n191: inline void convolution_shape_check(\n192:     CheckedFrom c,\n193:     const check_args(c, padding, input->dim() - 2, \"padding\");\n197:   check_args(c, stride, padding.size(), \"stride\");\n198:   check_args(c, dilation, padding.size(), \"dilation\");\n199: \n200:   // // NB: conv_output_size and conv_input_size are not bijections,\n213: // as conv_output_size loses information; this is why conv_input_size\n214: // takes an extra output_padding argument to resolve the ambiguity.\n215: \n216: template <typename T>\n217: inline std::vector<T> _conv_output_size(\n218:     ArrayRef<T> input_size, ArrayRef<T> weight_size,\n219:     ArrayRef<T> padding, ArrayRef<T> dilation\nstatic void check_args(CheckedFrom c, IntArrayRef args, size_t expected_size, const char* arg_name)\n{\n  TORCH_CHECK(args.size() <= expected_size,\n           \"Too many \", arg_name, \" However, writing a single function that does everything\n// means we get to reuse it for both forwards and all backwards\n// variants, even when the set of \"real\" inputs varies.  The magic of\n// relational computing!\n//\n// (There is one downside, which is that it is slightly harder to write\n// error messages which are able to distinguish between real inputs\n// (which the user can change) and computed inputs (which the user can\n// only indirectly affect).  It would be an interesting exercise to\n// come up with a general framework to handle such situations.)\ninline void convolution_shape_check(\n     CheckedFrom c,\n     const TensorGeometryArg& input, \"padding\");\n  check_args(c, stride, padding.size(), \"stride\");\n  check_args(c, dilation, padding.size(), \"dilation\");\n\n  // Input\n  checkDimRange(c, input, 3, 6 /* exclusive */);\n  checkSize_symint(c, input, input_channels_dim, weight->size(1) * groups);\n\n  // Weight\n  checkSameDim(c, input, weight);\n\n  // TODO: check that output->size() matches output_sizes\n  // TODO: has_dilation = !dilation.empty();\n  auto dim = input_size.size();\n  std::vector<T> output_size(dim);\n  output_size[0] = input_size[input_batch_size_dim];\n  output_size[1] = weight_size[weight_output_channels_dim];\n  for (const auto d : c10::irange(2, dim)) {\n    auto dilation_ = has_dilation ? dilation[d - 2] : 1;\n    auto kernel = dilation_ * (weight_size[d] - 1) + 1;\n    output_size[d] = (input_size[d] + (2 * padding[d - 2]) - kernel) / stride[d - 2] + 1;\n  }\n  return output_size;\n}\n\ninline std::vector<int64_t> conv_output_size(\n     IntArrayRef \\n199: template<typename scalar_t, typename param_t, template<typename T> class VarTransform>\\n200: static std::tuple<Tensor,Tensor> batch_norm_cpu_update_stats_template(\\n201:     const Tensor& input, const Tensor& running_mean, const Tensor& running_var,\\n202:     double momentum, double eps, Tensor& save_mean, Tensor& save_var_transform) {\\n203: \\n204:   using accscalar_t = \\n223:   auto running_mean_a = conditional_accessor_1d<param_t>(running_mean);\\n224:   auto running_var_a = conditional_accessor_1d<param_t>(running_var);\\n225: \\n226:   if (all_contiguous) _mean.accessor<opmath_t, 1>();\\n230:     auto _var_sum_a = _var_sum.accessor<opmath_t, 1>();\\n231:     auto momentum_ = static_cast<opmath_t>(momentum);\\n232: \\n233: \\n289: template<typename scalar_t, typename param_t, template<typename T> class VarTransform>\\n290: static std::tuple<Tensor,Tensor> batch_norm_cpu_update_stats_template(\\n291:     const Tensor& \\n199: template<typename scalar_t, typename param_t, template<typename T> class VarTransform>\\n200: static std::tuple<Tensor,Tensor> batch_norm_cpu_update_stats_template(\\n201:     const Tensor& input, const Tensor& running_mean, const Tensor& running_var,\\n202:     double momentum, double eps, Tensor& save_mean, Tensor& save_var_transform) {\\n203: \\n204:   using accscalar_t = \\n223:   auto running_mean_a = conditional_accessor_1d<param_t>(running_mean);\\n224:   auto running_var_a = conditional_accessor_1d<param_t>(running_var);\\n225: \\n226:   if (all_contiguous) {\\n227:     auto _mean = at::empty({n_input}, input.options().dtype(dtype));\\n228:     auto _var_sum = at::empty({n_input}, input.options().dtype(dtype));\\n229:     auto _mean_a = _mean.accessor<opmath_t, 1>();\\n230:     auto _var_sum_a = _var_sum.accessor<opmath_t, 1>();\\n231:     auto momentum_ = static_cast<opmath_t>(momentum);\\n232: \\n233:     batch_norm_cpu_collect_stats_stub(kCPU, _mean, _var_sum, input);\\n234: \\n235:     parallel_for(0, n_input, 1, [&](int64_t b_begin, int64_t b_end) {\\n236:       for (const auto f : });\\n249: \\n250:     return std::make_tuple(save_mean, save_var_transform);\\n251:   }\\n252: \\n253:   // non-contiguous path\\n254:   auto channel_stride = input.strides()[1];\\n255:   auto .declare_static_shape(input.sizes(), /*squash_dims=*/1)\\n260:       .check_all_same_dtype(false)\\n261:       .promote_inputs_to_common_dtype(false)\\n262:       .build();\\n263: \\n264:   parallel_for(0, n_input, 1, [&](int64_t b_begin, int64_t b_end) {\\n265:     TensorIterator iter(reduce_iter);\\n266:     for (const auto f : c10::irange(b_begin, b_end)) {\\n267:       // compute \\n289: template<typename scalar_t, typename param_t, template<typename T> class VarTransform>\\n290: static std::tuple<Tensor,Tensor> batch_norm_cpu_update_stats_template(\\n291:     const Tensor& input, const Tensor& running_mean, const Tensor& running_var,\\n292:     double momentum, double eps) {\\n293:   int64_t n_input = input.size(1);\\n294:   const int64_t ndim = input.dim();\\n295: std::tuple<Tensor,Tensor> batch_norm_cpu_update_stats_template(\n     const Tensor& input, const Tensor& running_mean, const Tensor& running_var,\n     double momentum, double eps, Tensor& save_mean,       if (running_var.defined()) {\n          accscalar_t unbiased_var = _var_sum_a[f] / (n - 1);\n          running_var_a[f] = momentum_ * unbiased_var + (1 - momentum_) * running_var_a[f];\n        }\n      }\n    });\n\n    return std::make_tuple(save_mean, save_var_transform);\n  }\n\n  // non-contiguous path\n  auto channel_stride = input.strides()[1];\n  auto in_data = .check_all_same_dtype(false)\n      .promote_inputs_to_common_dtype(false)\n      .build();\n\n  parallel_for(0, n_input, 1, [&](int64_t b_begin, int64_t b_end) {\n    TensorIterator momentum) * running_mean_a[f];\n      }\n      if (running_var.defined()) {\n        accscalar_t unbiased_var = var_sum / (n - 1);\n        running_var_a[f] = momentum * unbiased_var + (1 - momentum) * running_var_a[f];\n      }\n    }\n  });\n  return std::make_tuple(save_mean, save_var_transform);\n}\n\ntemplate<typename scalar_t, typename param_t, template<typename T> class VarTransform>\nstatic std::tuple<Tensor,Tensor> batch_norm_cpu_update_stats_template(\n     const Tensor& input, const Tensor& running_mean, const Tensor& running_var,\n     double momentum, double eps) {\n  int64_t n_input = input.size(1);\n  const int64_t ndim = input.dim();\n  DimVector reduce_dims(ndim - 1);\n  reduce_dims[0] = 0;\n  for (const auto i : c10::irange(2, ndim)) {\n    reduce_dims[i - 1] = i;\n  }\n\n  constexpr bool mixed_type = !std::is_same_v<scalar_t, param_t>;\n  const auto dtype = mixed_type ? kFloat : input.scalar_type();\n  Tensor save_mean = save_var_transform);\n}\n\ntemplate<typename scalar_t, typename param_t>\nstatic std::tuple<Tensor, Tensor, Tensor> batch_norm_backward_cpu_template(\n     const Tensor& grad_out_, const Tensor& eps) {\n  int64_t n_input = input.size(1);\n  const int64_t ndim = input.dim();\n  DimVector reduce_dims(ndim - 1);\n  reduce_dims[0] = 0;\n  for (const auto i : c10::irange(2, ndim)) {\n    reduce_dims[i - 1] = i;\n  }\n\n  constexpr bool mixed_type = !std::is_same_v<scalar_t, param_t>;\n  const auto dtype = mixed_type ? kFloat : input.scalar_type();\n  Tensor save_mean = is_contiguous(input) ? at::empty({n_input}, input.options().dtype(dtype)) : at::mean(input, /*dim=*/reduce_dims, /*keepdim=*/false, dtype);\n  Tensor save_var_transform = at::empty({n_input}, input.options().dtype(dtype));\n  return batch_norm_cpu_update_stats_template<scalar_t, param_t, VarTransform>(input, running_mean, running_var, momentum, eps, save_mean, save_var_transform);\n}\n\ntemplate<typename scalar_t, typename param_t>\nstatic std::tuple<Tensor, Tensor, Tensor> batch_norm_backward_cpu_template(\n     const Tensor& grad_out_, const Tensor& input, const Tensor& weight,\n     const Tensor& running_mean, const Tensor& running_var, const Tensor& save_mean, const Tensor& save_invstd,\n     bool train, double eps, std::array<bool,3> grad_input_mask) {\n\n  using accscalar_t = at::acc_type<scalar_t, false>;\n\n  constexpr bool mixed_type = !std::is_same_v<scalar_t, param_t>;\n  const auto dtype = mixed_type ? kFloat : input.scalar_type();\n\n  Tensor grad_input;\n  Tensor grad_weight;\n  Tensor grad_bias;\n  if (grad_input_mask[0]) {\n    grad_input = at::empty_like(input, input.suggest_memory_format());\n  }\n  if (grad_input_mask[1]) {\n    grad_weight = at::empty({input.size(1)}, input.options().dtype(dtype));\n  }\n  if (grad_input_mask[2]) {\n    grad_bias = at::empty({input.size(1)}, input.options().dtype(dtype));\n  }\n\n  // since we are directly manipulating pointers in contiguous path,\n  // need to make sure input and grad_out have the same memory format.\n  bool all_contiguous = is_contiguous(input)\n      && is_contiguous(grad_out_)\n      && input.suggest_memory_format() == grad_out_.suggest_memory_format();\n\n  if (all_contiguous) {\n    if (grad_input_mask[0]) {\n      grad_input = at::empty_like(input, suggest_memory_format_contig(input));\n    }\n    batch_norm_cpu_backward_stub(kCPU, grad_input, grad_weight, grad_bias,\n        grad_out_, input, weight, running_mean, running_var, save_mean, save_invstd, train, eps);\n    return std::make_tuple(grad_input, grad_weight, grad_bias);\n  }\n\n  auto weight_a = conditional_accessor_1d<const param_t>(weight);\n  auto grad_weight_a = conditional_accessor_1d<param_t>(grad_weight);\n  auto grad_bias_a = conditional_accessor_1d<param_t>(grad_bias);\n\n  int64_t n_input = input.size(1);\n  int64_t n = input.numel() / n_input;\n\n  auto save_mean_a = conditional_accessor_1d<const param_t>(save_mean);\n  auto save_invstd_a = conditional_accessor_1d<const param_t>(save_invstd);\n\n  auto running_mean_a = conditional_accessor_1d<const param_t>(running_mean);\n  auto running_var_a = conditional_accessor_1d<const param_t>(running_var);\n\n  const int64_t ndim = input.dim();\n\n  // Reduce all dimensions except dim=1\n  DimVector reduce_dims(ndim - 1);\n  reduce_dims[0] = 0;\n  for (const auto i : c10::irange(2, ndim)) {\n    reduce_dims[i - 1] = i;\n  }\n  // Using float data type for Half sum to avoid overflow\n  // since the representation range of Half is small.\n  auto sum = grad_out_.scalar_type() == kHalf\n      ? at::sum(grad_out_.to(ScalarType::Float), /*dim=*/reduce_dims)\n      : at::sum(grad_out_, /*dim=*/reduce_dims);\n  using sum_t = std::conditional_t<std::is_same_v<scalar_t, at::Half>, float, scalar_t>;\n  auto sum_a = sum.accessor<sum_t, 1>();\n\n  auto reduce_iter = TensorIteratorConfig()\n      .add_const_input(input)\n      .add_const_input(grad_out_)\n      .resize_outputs(false)\n      .declare_static_shape(input.sizes(), /*squash_dims=*/1)\n      .build();\n\n  TensorIterator unary_iter;\n  TensorIterator binary_iter;\n  if (grad_input_mask[0]) {\n    unary_iter.build(\n         TensorIteratorConfig()\n         .add_output(grad_input)\n         .add_const_input(train ? input : grad_out_)\n         .resize_outputs(false)\n         .declare_static_shape(input.sizes(), /*squash_dims=*/1));\n\n    if (train) {\n      binary_iter.build(\n          TensorIteratorConfig()\n          .add_output(grad_input)\n          .add_input(grad_input)\n          .add_const_input(grad_out_)\n          .resize_outputs(false)\n          .declare_static_shape(input.sizes(), /*squash_dims=*/1));\n    }\n  }\n\n  auto in_channel_stride = input.strides()[1];\n  auto in_data = input.const_data_ptr<scalar_t>();\n  auto grad_in_channel_stride = grad_input_mask[0] ? grad_input.strides()[1] : 0;\n  auto grad_in_data = grad_input_mask[0] ? grad_input.mutable_data_ptr<scalar_t>() : nullptr;\n  auto grad_out_channel_stride = grad_out_.strides()[1];\n  auto grad_out_data = grad_out_.const_data_ptr<scalar_t>();\n\n  parallel_for(0, n_input, 1, [&](int64_t b_begin, int64_t b_end) {\n      TensorIterator reduce_iter_local(reduce_iter);\n      TensorIterator unary_iter_local(unary_iter);\n      TensorIterator binary_iter_local(binary_iter);\n\n      for (const auto f : c10::irange(b_begin, b_end)) {\n        param_t w = weight.defined() ? weight_a[f] : param_t(1);\n\n        param_t mean{}, invstd{};\n        if (train) {\n          mean = save_mean_a[f];\n          invstd = save_invstd_a[f];\n        } else {\n          mean = running_mean_a[f];\n          invstd = 1 / std::sqrt(running_var_a[f] + eps);\n        }\n\n        // dot product of the Q(X) and gradOutput\n        accscalar_t dotp = 0;\n        reduce_iter_local.unsafe_replace_operand(\n             0, const_cast<scalar_t*>(in_data + f * in_channel_stride));\n        reduce_iter_local.unsafe_replace_operand(\n             1, const_cast<scalar_t*>(grad_out_data + f * grad_out_channel_stride));\n\n        cpu_serial_kernel(reduce_iter_local, [&](const scalar_t i, const scalar_t go) -> void {\n          dotp += (i - mean) * go;\n        });\n\n        if (grad_input_mask[0]) {\n          if (train) {\n            // when in training mode\n            // Q(X) = X - E[x] ; i.e. input centered to zero mean\n            // Y = Q(X) / sigma    ; i.e. BN output before weight and bias\n            // dL/dX = (Q(dL/dY) - dot(Y, dL/dY) * Y) / sigma * w\n\n            // projection of gradOutput on to output scaled by std\n            scalar_t k = (scalar_t) dotp * invstd * invstd / n;\n            {\n              unary_iter_local.unsafe_replace_operand(\n                  0, grad_in_data + f * grad_in_channel_stride);\n              unary_iter_local.unsafe_replace_operand(\n                  1, const_cast<scalar_t*>(in_data + f * in_channel_stride));\n              cpu_serial_kernel(unary_iter_local, [&](const scalar_t i) -> scalar_t {\n                return (i - mean) * k;\n              });\n            }\n\n            scalar_t grad_mean = sum_a[f] / n;\n            {\n              auto gI_data = grad_in_data + f * grad_in_channel_stride;\n              binary_iter_local.unsafe_replace_operand(0, gI_data);\n              binary_iter_local.unsafe_replace_operand(1, gI_data);\n              binary_iter_local.unsafe_replace_operand(\n                  2, const_cast<scalar_t*>(grad_out_data + f * grad_out_channel_stride));\n              cpu_serial_kernel(binary_iter_local, [&](scalar_t gi, scalar_t go) -> scalar_t {\n                return (go - grad_mean - gi) * invstd * w;\n              });\n            }\n          } else {\n            // when in evaluation mode\n            // Q(X) = X - running_mean  ; i.e. input centered to zero mean\n            // Y = Q(X) / running_std    ; i.e. BN output before weight and bias\n            // dL/dX = w / running_std\n            {\n              unary_iter_local.unsafe_replace_operand(\n                  0, grad_in_data + f * grad_in_channel_stride);\n              unary_iter_local.unsafe_replace_operand(\n                  1, const_cast<scalar_t*>(grad_out_data + f * grad_out_channel_stride));\n              cpu_serial_kernel(unary_iter_local, [&](const scalar_t i) -> scalar_t {\n                return i * invstd * w;\n              });\n            }\n          }\n        }\n        if (grad_input_mask[1]) {\n          grad_weight_a[f] = dotp * invstd;\n        }\n\n        if (grad_input_mask[2]) {\n          grad_bias_a[f] = sum_a[f];\n        }\n      }\n    });\n  return std::make_tuple(grad_input, grad_weight, grad_bias);\n}\n\nBatchNormBackend _select_batch_norm_backend(\n     const Tensor& input, const Tensor& weight, const Tensor& bias, const >= 3)\n      && ((input.sym_size(0) <= 880801 && training) // spatial, training\n          ||(input.sym_size(0) <= 65535 && !training)) //spatial, eval\n      && detail::getCUDAHooks().compiledWithCuDNN()\n      && eps >= detail::getCUDAHooks().batchnormMinEpsilonCuDNN()\n      && cudnn_enabled && detail::getCUDAHooks().versionRuntimeCuDNN() >= 5110L\n      && input.sym_numel() < std::numeric_limits<std::int32_t>::max() // some cuDNN kernels have 32-bit indexing limitations\n  ) {\n    return BatchNormBackend::Cudnn;\n  }\n\n  // TODO: Remove PYTORCH_MIOPEN_SUGGEST_NHWC_BATCHNORM once ROCm officially supports NHWC in MIOpen\n  // See https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/64427.\n  // non static variable is used to be able to change
